item_1.note: In the matter of Brasher v. Walgreens (McLean 24-CI-00012), the case caption shows Case: Kimberly-Brasher-Premise-2-25-2023 with client Kimberly Brasher. The record reflects a sequence of email communications between W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, and Matthew B. Steinberg, Co-Managing Partner at Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., concerning scheduling and discovery in the Brasher v. Walgreens matter. The communication was dated July 29, 2025, 03:59:50 GMT-04:00, and included a line from the client: “That is fine thank you.” The note also lists the sending and receiving parties, with Bryce Koon’s contact information and firm address, and the standard confidentiality disclaimer typical of the firm’s electronic communications. CC’d on the exchanges were Kimberly Brasher Premise 2/25/2023 – Filevine Project Email Address, Steven P. Stadler, and Inga A. Fonov, among others.

The first substantive exchange within the thread occurs on July 1, 2025, when Bryce Koon writes to Matt Steinberg asking, “Counsel, We would like to take the deposition of your corporate representative. Please provide me with potential dates in August and I will get back to you with a notice and list of topics. If you have any questions in this regard, please let me know.” This message is followed by Bryce’s closing and his firm’s signature block.

Earlier that same day, July 1, 2025 at 4:32 PM, Matt Steinberg replies to Bryce, with copies to the same recipients, explaining that they are required to submit to the Court an Agreed Scheduling Order and asking for any changes or authorization to file the attached draft with the Court and sign on the other party’s behalf. He notes his willingness to adjust dates as needed and asks for confirmation to proceed.

In a prior July 1, 2025 message (11:05 AM), Bryce had requested potential August deposition dates for the corporate representative and invited Matt to propose topics. The thread shows continued coordination on whether to pursue a corporate representative deposition and how that would fit with the case’s circumstances, including the store being closed at the time the client fell in the vacant parking lot.

On July 25, 2025, at 2:51 PM, Matt Steinberg sent another message to Bryce with a draft Agreed Scheduling Order and invited any changes. The email was again cc’d to Kimberly Brasher Premise 2/25/2023 – Filevine Project Email Address, Steven P. Stadler, and Inga A. Fonov, and included Matt’s firm signature and standard firm contact information. He signaled that he was sending the draft for review and alignment on discovery, experts, motions, pretrials, and trial dates.

Subsequently, on July 29, 2025, at 7:56 AM, Matt Steinberg sent a follow-up email reiterating the draft Agreed Scheduling Order and asking for any changes. At 3:34 PM the same day, Matt sent another message beginning with, “How does this work?” and stated that he was following up on the attached scheduling order draft, offering to adjust any dates, and requesting permission to file the document with the Court and sign the other party’s name if there were no changes. He again included his professional signature and firm information. The thread also preserves the broader firm boilerplate and client-support language, emphasizing the firm’s commitment to client service, and reiterates the confidentiality notice common to electronic communications.

The chain’s closing reflects the ongoing process: Bryce had solicited August deposition dates for a corporate representative and topics; Matt had proposed an Agreed Scheduling Order and offered to file it with the Court if the other side agreed or consented to signing on their behalf; and the parties remained engaged in discussions about discovery responses (noting that Matt had emailed Aaron with no response) and about whether a corporate representative deposition was appropriate given the store’s closure at the time of the incident, potentially requiring Court involvement. The record captures multiple drafts and correspondence aimed at establishing a scheduling order and moving the case forward through discovery, experts, motions, pretrials, and trial planning.

Re: Brasher v. Walgreens (McLean 24-CI-00012)

On July 1, 2025, at approximately 11:05 AM, Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm emailed Matthew B. Steinberg of Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., regarding Brasher v. Walgreens (McLean 24-CI-00012). In the message, Bryce stated that counsel would like to take the deposition of the corporate representative and asked Matthew to provide potential dates in August, promising to respond with a notice and a list of topics. The message was sent to Matthew with Kimberly Brasher Premise 2/25/2023 - Filevine Project Email Address in the cc line, along with Steven P. Stadler and Inga A. Fonov. The email included Bryce’s phone number and firm address, and ended with the standard attorney-client privilege disclaimer noting that the message is intended only for the named recipient and should not be forwarded; if received in error, recipients were instructed to contact The Whaley Law Firm and to preserve privilege.

Later on July 1, 2025, at about 4:32 PM, Matthew B. Steinberg replied to Bryce. He acknowledged the need to submit to the Court an Agreed Scheduling Order and indicated that he was attaching a draft scheduling order, expressing willingness to adjust any dates as needed. He asked Bryce to advise of any changes or whether he had Bryce’s permission to file the order with the Court and sign Bryce’s name on it. Matthew’s signature block followed, including his title as Co-Managing Partner of the Lexington Office of Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., and his contact information. The message also carried the standard advisory about the firm’s commitment to client service.

On July 25, 2025, at 2:51 PM, Matthew B. Steinberg sent another message to Bryce, with Kimberly Brasher Premise 2/25/2023 - Filevine Project Email Address, Steven P. Stadler, and Inga A. Fonov in copy. He attached a draft Agreed Scheduling Order and invited Bryce to advise of any changes. The email included Matthew’s firm signature block and the firm’s boilerplate about client experience and availability of client support.

Finally, on July 29, 2025, at 10:27 AM, Bryce Koon responded to Matthew. Bryce stated that he was agreeable to the structure of the agreed order but requested that the dates be moved back by 30 days. He indicated that if those changes were acceptable, Matthew had his permission to file the order; if not, Bryce asked to be informed. The message concluded with Bryce’s signature, The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information, and the same standard confidentiality disclaimer as the prior messages, noting that the email is intended for the named recipient and should not be used or forwarded to others if received in error.

item_9.note: In the Brasher v. Walgreens matter (McLean 24-CI-00012), pertaining to client Kimberly Brasher, a sequence of email correspondences took place in early July 2025 concerning discovery and a corporate representative deposition. The top message in the thread, dated July 3, 2025 at 11:28:44 a.m. Eastern Time, was from W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, addressed to Matthew B. Steinberg, Esq., with copies to Kimberly Brasher Premise 2/25/2023 – Filevine Project Email Address, Steven P. Stadler, Inga A. Fonov, and others. In this email, counsel thanked the recipient for the follow-up and stated that the discovery responses would be provided in the coming days. Regarding the Rule 30(b)(6) deposition, Koon outlined that the topics would address control and maintenance of the property after closure, any inspections or upkeep performed, the presence or absence of signage or warnings, and Walgreens’ general policies for closed locations. The email also indicated that the parties would cover whether any steps were taken to evaluate or document the condition of the premises before or after the incident. Koon acknowledged the opposing position but argued that these topics are appropriate for corporate testimony under the circumstances. He offered to share the finalized topic list and to discuss any concerns before proceeding with notice of the deposition. The email closed with Koon’s signature, including his title, The Whaley Law Firm, and contact details (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; phone [PHONE-14]; fax [PHONE-15]), followed by a standard privilege disclaimer noting that the message is intended only for the named recipient and warning against disclosure if received in error; a note about no waiver of privilege, and instructions not to forward the information to unintended recipients. An image note stating “Image removed by sender” appeared in the message.

Earlier that same day, July 1, 2025, at 11:05 a.m., Bryce Koon had sent another email in the same thread to Matthew B. Steinberg with Kimberly Brasher Premise 2/25/2023 – Filevine Project Email Address copied on the distribution list. In that message, Koon asked for potential dates in August to depose the corporate representative, stating that he would follow up with a notice and a list of topics once dates were proposed. He invited any questions in this regard and again signed with his contact information for The Whaley Law Firm.

That evening, at 4:31 p.m. on July 1, 2025, Matthew B. Steinberg replied to Bryce Koon. Steinberg noted that he had sent several emails to Aaron that had gone unanswered. He recounted that he had asked in April whether the parties would be open to negotiating an agreed scheduling order governing discovery, experts, motions, pretrial matters, and trial dates, and that he had sent a second request on June 12 seeking responses to discovery served in September. Steinberg stated that he did not see those responses and asked that they be produced within the next seven days. Regarding the proposed corporate representative deposition, he indicated that the topics would need to be appropriate for such a deposition given that Walgreens’ store was closed at the time the client fell in the vacant parking lot; depending on the topics, the matter might require discussion with the Court. He expressed willingness to discuss the matter over a call. He concluded by noting that if the parties preferred not to enter into a scheduling order, he would proceed with filing a Motion for a Status Conference with the Court to obtain dates on the calendar. The message closed with his signature block, listing his title as Co-Managing Partner – Lexington Office, Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., along with the firm’s Lexington address (444 East Main Street Suite 201, Lexington, KY 40507), phone, fax, and web address, and a broad list of jurisdictions where the firm operates. The message also included the firm’s standard client-support note and the same attorney-client privilege disclaimer that preceded the earlier communications.

In sum, the parties were coordinating discovery and a potential corporate deposition in the Brasher v. Walgreens case, with Koon proposing August deposition dates and outlining a 30(b)(6) topic list focused on post-closure property control and maintenance, inspections, signage or warnings, and Walgreens’ policies for closed locations, while Steinberg pressed for production of outstanding discovery responses and signaled possible Court involvement if scheduling could not be agreed. The exchange also reflected ongoing concerns about whether a corporate representative deposition would be appropriate given Walgreens’ store status at the time of the incident, and it included the customary disclaimers and contact details typical of the parties’ communications.

item_14.note: Case: Kimberly Brasher (Premise 2-25-2023). Client: Kimberly Brasher. This case concerns the claim identified as 20240514-001078 and involves The Phia Group, LLC, The Whaley Law Firm, and Ms. Brasher.

In late November 2024, The Phia Group’s Sarah Ingle took over the handling of Ms. Brasher’s file. On November 26, 2024, she advised that she had removed all claims marked “claim watcher LLC” from the listing and had requested additional information from the claims department for claims marked “Provider Unknown.” She stated that, as soon as she received a response, she would forward an updated lien. On November 27, 2024, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm replied, thanking Sarah for the update and saying she would update their contact information and look forward to further communication.

On December 3, 2024, Sarah Ingle sent the claim forms with additional provider information to Sarena Tuttle and indicated that she could provide anything else needed. She also included a note to mail all checks to P.O. Box 499, Canton, MA 02021. Sarena’s reply on December 4, 2024 acknowledged receipt and stated that the information would be treated as related. However, she noted two charges dated March 10 and March 12 from an “Unknown Provider” for the same amount of $17,270.50. She asked whether these charges were duplicative or whether the same procedure had been performed twice—once at the beginning and again at the end of Ms. Brasher’s inpatient hospitalization from March 10 through March 12. Sarena signed with her updated contact information, noting a new email address.

Throughout this period, standard confidentiality and privilege notices accompanied the communications. The emails and their attachments contained numerous disclaimers indicating that the information was confidential, intended only for the named recipient, not a substitute for legal advice, and not creating an attorney-client relationship unless expressly stated.

Moving forward to early 2025, on February 25, 2025, W. Bryce Koon, Esq., of The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to Sarena Tuttle (with Sarah Ingle copied) stating that they were actively trying to resolve Ms. Brasher’s claim and requesting a final lien amount related to Ms. Brasher’s treatment. Bryce provided his contact details and asked for the final lien amount.

On February 27, 2025, Cheyenne Lopes, a Sr. Contested Liability Specialist at The Phia Group, sent an updated listing of claims paid on behalf of the plan participant for which the Plan seeks reimbursement. She asked for notification if there were any other claims not included on the list and stated that, as long as Ms. Brasher is no longer treating, there would be no missing claims and everything should match the client’s records, allowing the matter to be treated as final. She also instructed that any outstanding balances should be rectified directly with the providers. The message included Cheyenne’s direct line and email, and represented that this could finalize the matter if there were no further discrepancies. Sarah Ingle subsequently forwarded this message in a reply to Cheyenne, continuing the discussion regarding the final lien and related claims.

In sum, the case progressed through late 2024 with internal reviews of claims lists, removal of certain claims, and questions about two duplicate/unknown-provider charges totaling $17,270.50 tied to the inpatient hospitalization period. By February 27, 2025, the parties were working toward a final lien amount and a final accounting of paid claims, with the understanding that the matter could be treated as final if no additional claims were missing and all records matched, provided outstanding balances were resolved with providers.

The next recommended step is to schedule a conference with the client to discuss mediation expectations, address concerns about settlement value, and prepare her for the upcoming mediation session.

item_46.note: Case: Kimberly Brasher v Walgreens Co. – McLean County, 24-CI-00012 – Mediation Scheduling

In early January 2025, the matter of Kimberly Brasher v Walgreens Co. in McLean County (case number 24-CI-00012) moved into mediation scheduling with Hon. Thomas Knopf selected as the mediator. The Whaley Law Firm, representing Ms. Brasher, coordinated with Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., whose Lexington office is led by Co-Managing Partner Matthew B. Steinberg, regarding available mediation dates and whether a half-day or full-day session would be appropriate. The parties discussed conducting mediation via Zoom to minimize travel, with the adjuster required to participate remotely due to being in California.

The scheduling dialogue began on January 9, 2025, when Sarena Tuttle, the Whaley Law Firm’s litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager, reached out to Mr. Steinberg to confirm dates that Hon. Knopf and the client could accommodate. Sarena provided January 2025 dates (21, 22, 23, 24, 29, 30, 31) and February 2025 dates (3, 4, 7, 11, 13, 14, 20, 21, 25, 26, 27, 28) and asked whether a half-day would suffice or if a full day was preferable.

In response on January 9, 2025 at 3:49 PM, Mr. Steinberg indicated that mediation could be held on February 25th or 28th, noting that his adjuster would need to participate via Zoom due to being in California, while he could attend in person or via Zoom.

Later that day, and again on January 9, 2025 at 2:46 PM, Sarena reiterated to Mr. Steinberg that the team preferred February 25th, 2025, and suggested conducting the mediation via Zoom to avoid travel. She asked whether a full-day or half-day format was preferred and proposed a 1:00 PM start time if a half-day would be sufficient.

On January 10, 2025, Mr. Steinberg replied that a half-day would be more than sufficient. In a follow-up that same day, Sarena confirmed, “Awesome. Let’s do Feb 25th 2025 via Zoom so no one has to travel. Do you prefer a full or half day? If a half day will suffice, we can do a 1:00 PM start time.”

Sarena then concluded with, “Sounds good. I will get everything lined out with Hon. Knopf’s office. Thank you so much. Stay safe & warm.” Her signature indicated her role as Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s address (712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222), direct line (D: [PHONE-573]), main line (O: [PHONE-572] ext 104), and her new email address Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com.

For reference, Mr. Steinberg’s credentials were listed as Co-Managing Partner – Lexington Office of Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., located at 444 East Main Street, Suite 201, Lexington, KY 40507, with Ph: [PHONE-154] and Fax: [PHONE-570], and email [EMAIL-156] (Web: www.qpwblaw.com). The communications also included cc’d colleagues Bryce Koon and Aaron Whaley from The Whaley Law Firm.

In sum, the parties agreed to proceed with a mediation on February 25, 2025, conducted via Zoom, with a half-day format (starting at 1:00 PM if a half-day is chosen) to accommodate the California-based adjuster, and to have Hon. Thomas Knopf oversee the mediation. The Whaley Law Firm confirmed the plan and continued to coordinate with Knopf’s office.
item_46.note_summary: Brasher | Brasher v Walgreens Co. | 2025-01-10
item_46.project_name: Kimberly-Brasher-Premise-2-25-2023
item_46.uuid: 496c880b-e7e5-48e3-8a54-ba7ebac3e359
item_47.author_name: Sarena Tuttle
item_47.episode_type: imported
item_47.last_activity: 2025-01-10T00:00:00
item_47.note: Case: Kimberly Brasher v Walgreens Co. in McLean County, case number 24-CI-00012, regarding mediation scheduling for the Kimberly Brasher case. The client is Kimberly Brasher.

On January 9, 2025, Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, acting as Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager, emailed Matthew B. Steinberg of Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., with Mr. Koon’s request to schedule mediation and to confirm the mediator. They had selected Hon. Thomas Knopf as the mediator and included a list of dates when he and their offices/clients were available. The dates proposed for January 2025 were 21, 22, 23, 24, 29, 30, 31; for February 2025: 3, 4, 7, 11, 13, 14, 20, 21, 25, 26, 27, 28.

In reply, Matt Steinberg stated that they could do mediation on February 25th or February 28th. He noted that his adjuster would need to participate via Zoom because the adjuster is located in California, but he would attend either in person or by Zoom himself.

The following day, January 10, 2025, Sarena responded: they should proceed with February 25, 2025, via Zoom to minimize travel, and she asked whether a full or half day would be preferred. If a half day is chosen, she suggested a 1:00 PM start time.

He signed as Co-Managing Partner of the Lexington Office for Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., including his contact details.

Summary of key logistics confirmed or discussed across the emails:
- Case: Kimberly Brasher v Walgreens Co., McLean County, 24-CI-00012.
- Mediator: Hon. Thomas Knopf.
- Scheduling focus: Mediation to be held in February 2025, with February 25th as the preferred date, contending between February 25th or 28th for potential dates (the February 25th option was reiterated).

The matter involves Kimberly Brasher as the client, with litigation against Walgreen Co. The correspondence spans several weeks in November and December 2024. Steinberg, Esq., Co-Managing Partner of Quintairos, Prieto, Wood & Boyer, P.A., representing Walgreen Co. The messages include standard attorney-client privilege disclosures typical to electronic communications, stating the message is intended only for the named recipient and that any inadvertent receipt should be reported to the sending firm and not used or forwarded to others.

Chronology of discovery communications

- November 12, 2024. The first recorded email in the thread from this date shows Matthew B. Steinberg writing to Bryce Koon regarding progress on discovery. Steinberg notes that he has just received the file and will likely need a few days to understand what is happening, and asks if Bryce is okay with him responding by early next week, apologizing for any delay. - December 12, 2024. Bryce Koon follows up with Steinberg about the discovery requests in the case, asking for any updates. - December 13, 2024 (morning). His signature block is included with his contact information and firm branding. A prior header line shows a partial “From” and an “Error! Filename not specified.” note from the system.

- December 13, 2024 (later that morning). Bryce responds with a greeting, “Good morning Matthew,” and says, “Please see attached.” He provides a Dropbox link to relevant documents for the case: https://www.dropbox.com/scl/fi/tqrnzqyt94qf1ergchw4f/Brasher-Demand-Exhibits.pdf?rlkey=8lfk22d08o4z59ublt1q3ax6e&st=z9tiqqfc&dl=0. Bryce states that if there is trouble with the link or questions arise, he should be contacted. He includes his signature block and the standard privilege disclaimer. An image placeholder is noted as “Image removed by sender.” in the body of the message.

- December 23, 2024. Steinberg responds to the ongoing exchange, thanking the others and reporting that he has now gone through the file. He notes that “Lee had discovery complete and verified just before he transferred the file to me” and asks whether Lee ever served these responses on the other side. His message includes his signature block and the standard privilege disclaimer.

- December 27, 2024. Bryce Koon replies to Matthew Steinberg: “Good afternoon Matthew, We have not received any discovery responses that I am aware of.” He signs as W. Bryce Koon, Esq., The Whaley Law Firm, with the firm’s full address and contact numbers. The message includes the firm’s standard privilege disclaimer. The CC line for this message shows the ongoing referral of the Kimberly Brasher matter within the Filevine project and related project email address.

Additional case and submission context
The communications repeatedly reference discovery requests and the status of responses in the case. The subject line across the emails identifies the matter as “Kimberly Brasher v. Walgreen Co. (McLean 24-CI-00012).” The case is tracked under the header “Case: Kimberly-Brasher-Premise-2-25-2023” with the client listed as Kimberly Brasher. Several emails include or reference the Filevine project email address associated with Kimberly Brasher’s premise, which appears in the CC lines of multiple messages. Between November 12 and December 27, 2024, counsel for Kimberly Brasher and counsel for Walgreen Co. exchanged questions and updates about the progress, service, and provision of discovery responses in the case Kimberly Brasher v. Walgreen Co. (McLean 24-CI-00012). item_64.note: Case: Kimberly-Brasher-Premise-2-25-2023. Client: Kimberly Brasher. The note tracks an email chain about discovery requests from the defense counsel in Kimberly Brasher’s premise liability claim, with the subject line The Defense Counsel's Discovery Requests.

On November 27, 2024, Kimberly Brasher sent an email to Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm, with Bryce Koon copied, replying, “Thank you for the update. That is very helpful.”

In the prior day’s correspondence, November 26, 2024, Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, wrote to Kim explaining that she could understand Kim’s frustration with the process and apologizing for not having been better informed about how long litigation typically takes. She noted that a standard circuit court case can take two years or more, without snags or delays, and that Kim’s claim is on track with that timeline. She also mentioned that the defense had recently changed counsel and that they did not anticipate a significant delay for the new counsel to catch up. Mediation was anticipated in the Spring if the defense was open to settlement after they were caught up. Sarena advised Kim to inform medical providers who contact her that the bills are in pending litigation and to feel free to provide The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information to anyone attempting to collect them, to avoid garnishment or further issues. She reassured Kim that the firm could assist with those matters and invited any further questions. The message included Sarena’s signature block with her title, the firm’s name and address at 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222, and contact details: D: [PHONE-212], O: [PHONE-512] ext 104, E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, with a note indicating a NEW EMAIL ADDRESS.

Earlier, on November 25, 2024, at 3:56 PM, Kimberly Brasher wrote expressing that she was not aware of anyone’s retirement or the defense counsel changing, or anything else affecting the defendant’s response to her claim. She stated she expected hospitals and other medical providers to garnish her wages any day and emphasized an urgent interest in finding out whether there was progress toward settlement or not. She apologized for sounding pushy, explaining that she had started her claim over a year ago and was not expecting such a lengthy process.

That same day, at 8:41 AM, Sarena Tuttle replied to Kim, asking Kim to explain her previous statement and asking, “Who is suing you?” She noted that Kim’s deposition had been taken on October 1, 2024. She explained that the defense counsel had recently changed due to Mr. Sitlinger’s retirement and that they did not anticipate any significant movement in Kim’s case until after the New Year. She emphasized the need to allow the new counsel time to review the case and that, once they were caught up, they hoped to schedule mediation. However, she added that whether mediation could occur would depend on the new counsel’s position, and that The Whaley Law Firm would reach out to discuss the next steps once they heard back from the new counsel.

On Saturday, November 23, 2024, at 11:59 AM, Kimberly Brasher wrote, “Hi Serena. This is my second attempt to reach out for any information on my case before I just let all of WKy and southern IN sue me. Thanks.” She signed, “Kimberly K Brasher.”

Prior messages include Kim’s earlier notes: on Friday, November 8, 2024, at 9:17 AM, she asked if there had been any update or recent movement regarding her Walgreens case. On Monday, September 16, 2024, at 10:24 AM, Sarena Tuttle sent a message attaching the Discovery Requests from the Defense Counsel in Kim’s premise liability claim. She urged Kim to review the packet and call to discuss. Sarena acknowledged the packet could seem overwhelming but offered assistance in completing the task. She noted that several questions would not require answers because they were outside Kim’s scope of information (such as which experts would be called at trial) and that there were requests for document production. She added that most documents would already be in Kim’s file and she would not need to produce them a second time. The message concluded with Sarena’s signature block, including her role, the firm’s address, and contact information, and a note reiterating the “PLEASE NOTE NEW EMAIL ADDRESS.”

The communications consistently reference a Walgreens-related premise liability claim, with discussions about discovery requests, anticipated timelines, changes in defense counsel due to retirement, and expectations regarding mediation and settlement, as well as guidance for managing medical bills during pending litigation. The email chain also notes The Whaley Law Firm’s contact details and a new email address for Sarena.

item_66.note: Case: Kimberly-Brasher-Premise-2-25-2023. Client: Kimberly Brasher.

Initial client contact on November 26, 2024, with Sarena regarding the ongoing claim for Kimberly Brasher. The client had sent an email explaining that she was not aware of anyone’s retirement, the defense counsel changing, or any other factor that might be delaying the defendant’s response to her claim. She stated that she expects hospitals and other medical providers to place a garnishment on her almost immediately, which created an urgent need to know whether a settlement is closer or no settlement is anticipated. She noted that she is not in regular contact with the office and asked for some leeway if she sounded pushy, since she began her claim more than a year ago and did not anticipate such a lengthy process.

Reply to Client: Sarena replied to Kim with empathy and clarity. She acknowledged Kim’s frustration with the process and apologized for not keeping her better informed about how long litigation typically takes. She explained that a standard circuit court case can take about two years easily, absent snags or delays, and that Kim’s claim is currently on track with that general timeline. She noted that the defense had made a rapid change and that they do not anticipate a significant delay for the new counsel to get up to speed. Mediation was anticipated to be scheduled in the spring, provided the defense does not remain closed to settlement discussions once they are caught up. Regarding bills from medical providers, Kim was advised to inform them that the bills are in a pending litigation and to feel free to share the firm’s contact information with anyone attempting to collect them; she was cautioned not to let the bills go into collections or create further issues for herself, and the firm pledged to help with those matters. The message closed with an invitation for Kim to reach out with any additional questions or to discuss them in more detail.

Person Making Contact: Sarena
Date & Time: November 26, 2024

There will be several questions that you will not need to answer as they are outside your scope of information, such as which 'experts' we will call at trial. There are also requests for document production and we will have most of these documents already in your file and you will not need to produce them a 2nd time. On November 25, 2024, Sarena Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, sent an email to Kim Brasher in reference to the defense counsel’s discovery requests. The subject line read “Re: The Defense Counsel's Discovery Requests.” In the body, Sarena asked Kim to explain her statement and to identify who is suing her. She noted that Kim’s deposition had been taken on October 1, 2024. Sarena also explained that the defense counsel had recently changed because Mr. Sitlinger retired. She stated that they do not anticipate any significant movement that would involve Kim as a party until after the New Year, since the new counsel would need time to review the case. Once the new counsel is up to speed, they hoped to schedule a mediation, though this would depend on the position the new counsel takes on the claim. They would reach out to Kim to discuss the next steps once they heard back.

Tuttle.

Box 499, Canton, MA 02021 and must include the case number, and she closed with her manager Jamie Johnson’s contact information and a note that both she and Johnson value feedback.

On October 11, 2024 at 13:41:17 UTC, Sarah Bracken sent a final note stating that she would have the Phia Group claims department review to add all the claims and would discuss the matter once those were received. She noted she would be out of the office for the entire next week and would follow up upon her return. She again provided payment instructions (mail to P.O. Box 499, Canton, MA 02021, including the case number) and reiterated that her manager Jamie Johnson and she valued feedback. The email signature identified her as Senior Recovery Specialist for The Phia Group, LLC, with the phone/fax number [PHONE-473], and included standard branding and LinkedIn follow prompts.

Throughout the thread, multiple confidentiality and informational-use boilerplate notices appeared, repeatedly stating that the information is for informational purposes only, not a substitute for legal counsel, does not create an attorney-client relationship, and is confidential. Several of these notices were included in the messages at various points in the correspondence.

In sum, the communications between The Phia Group and The Whaley Law Firm regarding Kimberly Brasher’s case (20240514-001078) centered on identifying and adding missing dates of service to the lien (potentially involving Commonwealth Pain Associates), sharing and referencing the original October 1, 2024 correspondence and a complete treatment summary, and planning for the Phia Group’s claims department to review and add all claimed items, with ongoing coordination and standard payment procedures and contact details maintained throughout.

item_84.note: Chronology of communications regarding Kimberly Brasher’s lien (case reference 20240514-001078) documents a short, three-message exchange between The Phia Group and The Whaley Law Firm in early October 2024.

On October 4, 2024, at approximately 10:06 AM, Sarah Bracken of The Phia Group emailed Sarena Tuttle regarding Kimberly Brasher. Sarah noted that it appeared dates of service were missing from the latest lien list because some items had been coded for “joint disorder” rather than being specific to the hip. She asked whether these dates should be added from Commonwealth Pain Associates and asked for confirmation on whether all such records should be included.

On October 9, 2024, at 1:38 PM, Sarena M. Tuttle, a Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, replied. She apologized for the delayed response, explaining she had been out of the office at the end of the previous week. She confirmed that Sarah should include any and all records. She invited further questions or concerns to be discussed directly. Sarena provided her contact details: The Whaley Law Firm, 712 Lyndon Lane, Louisville, KY 40222; D: [PHONE-472]; O: [PHONE-254] ext 104; E: Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com, noting it as her new email address.

That same message contains the standard informational and confidentiality disclaimers typical of the correspondence. The notices make clear that the information is informational only, not a substitute for legal counsel, does not create an attorney-client relationship, and is confidential and intended only for the addressed entity. The Phia Group emphasizes that it is not a law firm and is not responsible for any claims coverage decisions or payment. The notices reiterate the need to seek licensed legal counsel and advise deletion if received in error. Similar language appears again in later notes.

On October 10, 2024, at 17:43:24 UTC, Sarah Bracken sent a follow-up email to Sarena. She stated that it may be easier to include the dates of service missing from the lien. Her closing included her full signature information: Senior Recovery Specialist, The Phia Group, LLC; Phone/Fax: [PHONE-255]; LinkedIn follow prompt. The email also provided two payment addresses that appeared in the thread, and a request to include the case number with payments: "PAYMENTS SHOULD BE MAILED TO, P.O. BOX 499, CANTON, MA 02021" (in this message) along with the case number. The message again referenced her manager, Jamie Johnson ([EMAIL-469]), and stated that both she and Jamie value the recipient’s feedback. Her signature line also included the standard business disclaimers that accompany the correspondence.

Additionally, the thread contains several embedded image references (cid:image001.png, cid:image002.png, cid:image003.png) associated with the October 10 message, indicating the presence of attached visuals in that email.

Throughout the correspondence, references appear to the same subject line: "Kimberly Brasher (20240514-001078" and/or "Re: Kimberly Brasher (20240514-001078." The communication trail also includes an earlier note about where payments should be mailed (P.O. Box 390, Canton, MA 02021) in the October 4 message, contrasted with the later instruction to mail payments to P.O. Box 499, Canton, MA 02021. The Phia Group’s branding elements, including “Follow Us On LinkedIn!” and the manager contact, Jamie Johnson, recur in the signatures.

In summary, the exchange shows a collaborative effort to ensure all relevant dates of service are captured for the lien, with The Whaley Law Firm requesting that all records be included, and The Phia Group seeking confirmation and offering guidance on where to send payment and whom to contact for feedback. The chain also includes multiple standard confidentiality and informational-use disclaimers and indicates a change in Sarena Tuttle’s listed email address to Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com.

The message included a standard attorney-client privilege and confidentiality disclaimer indicating that the email is intended only for the named recipient, that it may contain privileged information, and instructions to contact The Whaley Law Firm if received in error, with a note that no waiver of privilege applies and that the information should not be used or forwarded to others not intended to receive it. The email was a forwarded message.

Forwarded message:
From Sharon Archer, dated Friday, September 13, 2024, at approximately 12:25 PM, subject RE: Kimberly Brasher v. Walgreen Co., sent to [EMAIL-298] and [EMAIL-299] with Lee Sitlinger CC’d. 1) An Answer on behalf of Walgreen Co.;
2) Defendant Walgreen Co.’s First Set of Interrogatories Propounded to Plaintiff, Kimberly Brasher;

4) Notice of Service.

She invited any questions or issues opening the attachments and signed the message as Sharon K. Archer, Legal Assistant to Lee E. Sitlinger, SITLINGER LAW, 320 Whittington Parkway, Suite 304, Louisville, Kentucky 40222, email [EMAIL-425], telephone [PHONE-424] x 708, and fax [PHONE-423].

item_127.note: In the matter of Kimberly Brasher v. Walgreens Co., McLean Circuit Court No. 24-CI-00012, the parties began coordinating the deposition schedule for Ms. Kimberly Brasher and, if needed, Walgreens’ representative who oversaw the property and its maintenance. The exchange involved Sarena M. Tuttle, litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm, and Sharon K. Archer, legal assistant to Lee E. Sitlinger at Sitlinger Law, with Curt Sitlinger and Greg Whaley also copied on the thread.

The planning kicked off on July 16, 2024, when Sharon Archer informed Sarena that Walgreens would like to schedule the deposition for October, to be held in Walgreens’ office, and asked for Whaley’s availability in October, noting that availability should exclude October 16 through 25. A few minutes later, Sarena requested dates in September as well, but Sharon clarified that the start should be in October and thanked her. Sarena then asked for both offices’ availability in October so they could coordinate with Ms. Brasher and, later that day, Sharon acknowledged she would forward the request to Mr. Sitlinger, who was out of the office at the time, and said they would need to get back with a response. Sarena wrapped up that exchange by simply noting she appreciated the update.

On July 22, 2024, Sarena wrote again to Sharon and Curt Sitlinger, expressing appreciation for locating the best Walgreens representative for a deposition and noting that Mr. Koon was happy to schedule the deposition of Mrs. Brasher. With October fairly open in their calendar, she asked that Walgreens provide dates your office was available so those dates could be discussed with Mrs. Brasher.

The following day, July 23, 2024, Sharon provided Walgreens’ available dates for Ms. Brasher’s deposition: October 1, 4, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11, 14, 15, and 16. She asked for confirmation on which of those dates would work. Later that day, Sarena responded: October 1 at 10:00 a.m. sounded good. She added that if a Walgreens representative could be determined, they could be added in the afternoon if needed, and she asked whether a Zoom deposition would be preferable given that Mrs. Brasher lives about 2.5 hours away and the Walgreens representative’s location was still undetermined.

Throughout, the correspondence circulated among the following participants and roles:
- Sarena M. Tuttle, litigation paralegal and workers’ compensation case manager for The Whaley Law Firm, Louisville, KY.
- Sharon K. Archer, legal assistant to Lee E. Sitlinger at Sitlinger Law, Louisville, KY.
- Curt Sitlinger, attorney at Sitlinger Law.
- Greg Whaley, attorney at The Whaley Law Firm.
- Bryce Koon, associated with The Whaley Law Firm.

All communications reference the case’s procedural posture and the practical considerations of scheduling: confirming October as the target month, identifying available dates for Ms. Brasher’s deposition at Walgreens’ office (and possibly coordinating with a Walgreens representative), and evaluating the option of conducting the deposition by Zoom due to distance and the yet-undetermined location of the Walgreens representative.

item_134.note: In the matter of Kimberly Brasher v. Walgreen Co., et al. (McLean Circuit Court, No. 24-CI-00012), the scheduling of Ms. Kimberly Brasher’s deposition became the subject of a series of emails between counsel for Walgreens and counsel for the plaintiff, starting in mid-July 2024. On July 16, 2024, Sharon K. Archer, the legal assistant to Lee E. Sitlinger at Sitlinger Law, informed Sarena Tuttle of The Whaley Law Firm that Walgreens’ litigation team would like to schedule Ms. Brasher’s deposition for October in their office, requesting availability for any October dates other than October 16–25. Archer identified the matter as representing Walgreen Co. and provided contact details for her firm: Sitlinger Law, 320 Whittington Parkway, Suite 304, Louisville, Kentucky 40222; [EMAIL-380]; telephone [PHONE-381] x708; fax [PHONE-382].

Also on July 16, Sarena Tuttle replied seeking dates in September as a possibility and noting Walgreens’ preference to schedule for October, with the understanding that Sitlinger’s firm would provide availability for October 2024 to take Ms. Brasher’s deposition at their office, excluding Oct. 16–25. In the interim, she suggested coordinating with Walgreens’ representatives who oversaw the property and its maintenance to possibly appear on the same deposition date. Sharon Archer responded that she had forwarded the email to Mr. Sitlinger, who was currently out of the office, and that they would respond when he returned.

Later that same day, July 16, Sarena acknowledged Sharon’s update with a brief “Awesome. Thank you so much.” The email correspondence continued over the next several days, with Sharon explaining that Mr. Sitlinger would prefer to begin with October dates, and Sarena asking for the availability of Mr. Whaley or Mr. Koon in October 2024 to take Ms. Brasher’s deposition, noting the dates to avoid were October 16–25. The thread shows ongoing back-and-forth while Sitlinger was out of the office, and Sarena indicating a desire to align dates for Ms. Brasher’s deposition along with any Walgreens representatives’ deposition on the same day, if possible.

On July 22, 2024, Sarena sent a message reiterating appreciation for locating the appropriate Walgreens representative to handle the deposition and requesting an update once the information was obtained. She indicated that Mr. Bryce Koon of The Whaley Law Firm was happy to schedule the deposition of Ms. Brasher, and pointed out that October calendars were fairly open. She asked that Walgreens’ office provide dates they were available so she could discuss them with Ms. Brasher as soon as possible. The message was copied to relevant parties, including Greg Whaley and Bryce Koon.

Finally, on July 23, 2024, Sharon Archer responded with a list of October dates that were available for Ms. Brasher’s deposition: October 1, 4, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11, 14, 15, and 16. Archer asked to advise whether any of those dates would work for Walgreens’ office. Archer signed as the Legal Assistant to Lee E. Sitlinger of Sitlinger Law, providing her office’s contact information and address: SITLINGER LAW, 320 Whittington Parkway, Suite 304, Louisville, Kentucky 40222; [EMAIL-383]; telephone [PHONE-384] x708; fax [PHONE-385]. The message also lists the case details and indicates that the matter involves Walgreens Co., with depositions to be scheduled at the Sitlinger Law office, and references the deposition of the Walgreens representatives who oversaw the property and its maintenance. The exchange reflects ongoing coordination among The Whaley Law Firm (Sarena Tuttle, Curt Sitlinger, Greg Whaley, Bryce Koon) and Sitlinger Law (Sharon Archer) regarding timing and participants for the depositions in October.

item_136.note: Case: Kimberly-Brasher-Premise-2-25-2023. Client: Kimberly Brasher. This matter concerns Kimberly Brasher v. Walgreen Co., et al., in McLean Circuit Court, No. 24-CI-00012.

In a July 22, 2024 email, Sarena M. Tuttle, Litigation Paralegal and Workers’ Compensation Case Manager at The Whaley Law Firm, addressed Sharon Archer and Curt Sitlinger (with Greg Whaley and Bryce Koon copied) regarding depositions in the Walgreens litigation. She thanked them for locating the best person to represent Walgreens for a deposition and requested an update once that representation is identified. She advised that Mr. Koon is available to schedule the deposition of Mrs. Brasher and noted that their October calendar is fairly open; she asked Walgreens to provide dates their office is available so they could discuss those dates with Ms. Brasher promptly. Her signature included The Whaley Law Firm’s contact information, including the new email address Sarena@WhaleyLawFirm.com.

The email chain also shows the ongoing scheduling discussion from July 16, 2024. Early that morning, Sharon Archer of Sitlinger Law informed Sarena that Walgreens represents Walgreens in the matter and that Mr. Sitlinger would like to schedule the deposition of Kimberly Brasher for sometime in October at Sitlinger’s office, requesting availability in October 2024 for Brasher’s deposition, with the exclusion of October 16–25. Sarena replied that, while they preferred not to push the claim far into the future, they would likely want to schedule the Walgreens representatives—who oversaw the property and its maintenance—to be deposed on the same day as Brasher, and she asked for dates when both offices could be available.

Sharon then clarified that Sitlinger wished to begin with October dates, rather than September. She asked for Mr. Whaley’s or Mr. Koon’s availability in October 2024 to depose Ms. Brasher, with the exception of Oct. 16–25. In response, Sarena reiterated the request for October dates and, when appropriate, September dates as well. She provided her contact details and reiterated the preference to schedule the deposition on October dates.

The thread continued with a brief exchange indicating Sharon would forward the message to Mr. Sitlinger, who was out of the office, and that they would have to get back to Whaley Law regarding the email. Sarena thanked Sharon for the update. The correspondence reflects the parties’ efforts to coordinate the deposition of Kimberly Brasher and the Walgreens representatives on the same day, with October 2024 identified as the initial target window and October 16–25 excluding, along with a request for mutual availability.

The exchange concludes with the repeated note from Whaley on May 16, 2024, referencing the Sedgwick letter and the notion that Walgreens should be added as a defendant if the Sedgwick position persists, thereby aligning with the possibility of an Agreed Order substituting Walgreens for the time being.

item_287.note: Case: Kimberly Brasher – Premise 2-25-2023. Client: Kimberly Brasher.

On September 20, 2023, at 10:06 AM, Jessica Bottorff of The Whaley Law Firm emailed Deaconess Medical Records with the subject “Kimberly Brasher [EXTERNAL EMAIL]” and cc’d [EMAIL-711]. The body stated that attached was a request for records and bills on their client, Kimberly Brasher, and it was signed by The Whaley Law Firm. The email carried external-sender notices and security banners indicating it was an external email and advising caution with attachments or links.

The next day, September 21, 2023, at 7:58 AM, the message chain was forwarded to include a reply from Pamela Newman. In her original response dated September 20, 2023 at 4:13 PM, Ms. Newman informed the requester that the Authorization was not dated and instructed them to resubmit with a dated authorization. She added an important note: as of October 1, 2023, all requests would be pre-pay only and payment must be made before records would be released. She then provided the procedures for submitting future requests: send all records requests to Deaconess Midtown Hospital via fax at [PHONE-712] or to her email for faster service, noting that she processes requests for Deaconess Clinic’s, Deaconess Midtown Hospital, and Deaconess Gateway Hospital. Her signature block included the following details: Pamela J. Newman, ROI/Medical Records Specialist III; Email: [EMAIL-713]; Direct Line: [PHONE-714]; Legal Medical Records: [PHONE-715]; Fax: [PHONE-716]; and the mailing address 1419 W. Lloyd Expressway, Suite 101, Evansville, Indiana 47710.

The forwarded chain also included the original message from Jessica Bottorff stating, “Attached is a request for records & bills on our client, Kimberly Brasher,” and identified The Whaley Law Firm as the sender. The communications were labeled as external, and the chain contained standard external-email warnings and disclaimers regarding confidentiality.
